<div id="page0" style="width:611.9pt;height:791.8pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">05</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
<p style="top:85.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Trends in Modern Application Development</span></b></p>
<p style="top:127.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">As Platform as a Service (PaaS) and Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS) offerings have matured, </span></p>
<p style="top:144.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">software development and architecture patterns have shifted to meet new infrastructure </span></p>
<p style="top:161.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">paradigms. Cloud providers abstract the underlying hardware away, and applications must </span></p>
<p style="top:178.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">correspondingly be designed to handle failure and changes in this commodity computing </span></p>
<p style="top:195.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">infrastructure. Exposing application endpoints to publish health and metric data (with the </span></p>
<p style="top:212.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">expectation that these endpoints will be regularly polled and the data will be acted upon), as well </span></p>
<p style="top:229.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">as packaging applications in smaller, self-contained disposable pieces has become the new norm </span></p>
<p style="top:246.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">in developing resilient cloud-based applications.</span></p>
<p style="top:280.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Designing applications that will be rapidly and continuously deployed into cloud environments has </span></p>
<p style="top:297.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">led to the development of new software methodologies like &#x201c;Cloud Native&#x201d; and &#x201c;Twelve Factor.&#x201d; </span></p>
<p style="top:314.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">These high-level frameworks address common challenges in running scalable applications on </span></p>
<p style="top:331.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">cloud platforms and serve to guide software developers and architects in the design of resilient </span></p>
<p style="top:348.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and highly observable applications. Such frameworks build on recent developments in software </span></p>
<p style="top:365.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">engineering like containers, microservices-oriented architectures, continuous integration and </span></p>
<p style="top:382.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deployment, and automated orchestration.</span></p>
<p style="top:466.2pt;left:61.7pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Twelve Factor</span></b></p>
<p style="top:508.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Codebase</span></b></p>
<p style="top:525.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Dependencies</span></b></p>
<p style="top:542.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Con&#xfb01;g</span></b></p>
<p style="top:559.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Backing services</span></b></p>
<p style="top:576.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Build, release, run</span></b></p>
<p style="top:593.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Processes</span></b></p>
<p style="top:610.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Port binding</span></b></p>
<p style="top:627.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Concurrency</span></b></p>
<p style="top:644.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Disposability</span></b></p>
<p style="top:661.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Dev/prod parity</span></b></p>
<p style="top:678.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Logs</span></b></p>
<p style="top:695.2pt;left:91.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Admin processes</span></b></p>
<p style="top:506.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Synthesizing extensive experience developing and deploying apps </span></p>
<p style="top:523.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">onto their cloud PaaS, Heroku constructed a framework for building </span></p>
<p style="top:540.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">modern applications consisting of 12 development guidelines, </span></p>
<p style="top:557.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">conceived to increase developers&#x2019; productivity and improve the </span></p>
<p style="top:574.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">maintainability of applications.</span></p>
<p style="top:608.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">As PaaS providers abstract away all layers beneath the application, it </span></p>
<p style="top:625.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">is important to adapt the packaging, monitoring, and scaling of </span></p>
<p style="top:642.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">apps to this new level of abstraction. The Twelve Factors allow a </span></p>
<p style="top:659.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">move towards declarative, self-contained, and disposable services. </span></p>
<p style="top:676.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">When effectively leveraged, they form a uni&#xfb01;ed methodology for </span></p>
<p style="top:693.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">building and maintaining apps that are both scalable and easily </span></p>
<p style="top:710.7pt;left:216.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deployable, fully utilizing managed cloud infrastructure.</span></p>
<p style="top:508.2pt;left:76.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">I.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:525.2pt;left:73.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">II.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:542.2pt;left:69.9pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">III.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:559.2pt;left:69.6pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">IV.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:576.2pt;left:72.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">V.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:593.2pt;left:68.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">VI.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:610.2pt;left:65.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">VII.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:627.2pt;left:62.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">VIII.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:644.2pt;left:68.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">IX.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:661.2pt;left:71.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">X.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:678.2pt;left:68.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">XI.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:695.2pt;left:65.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">XII.</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:85.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Cloud Native</span></b></p>
<p style="top:126.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">As cloud platforms, infrastructure, and tooling have evolved and matured since the original Twelve </span></p>
<p style="top:143.1pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Factors were published, and large-scale cloud migrations and deployments informed the software </span></p>
<p style="top:159.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">development community, an extended and broader methodology called </span><i><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Cloud Native</span></i><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> has </span></p>
<p style="top:176.1pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">emerged. At a high level, Cloud Native apps are containerized, segmented into microservices, and </span></p>
<p style="top:192.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">are designed to be dynamically deployed and ef&#xfb01;ciently run by orchestration systems </span></p>
<p style="top:209.1pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">like Kubernetes.</span></p>
<p style="top:240.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">What makes an application Cloud Native?</span></b></p>
<p style="top:266.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">To effectively deploy, run, and manage Cloud Native apps, the application must implement several </span></p>
<p style="top:283.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Cloud Native best practices. For example, a Cloud Native app should:</span></p>
<p style="top:300.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Expose a health check endpoint so that container orchestration systems can probe </span></p>
<p style="top:317.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">application state and react accordingly</span></p>
<p style="top:334.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Continuously publish logging and telemetry data, to be stored and analyzed by systems like </span></p>
<p style="top:351.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Elasticsearch and Prometheus for logs and metrics, respectively</span></p>
<p style="top:368.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Degrade gracefully and cleanly handle failure so that orchestrators can recover by restarting </span></p>
<p style="top:385.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">or replacing it with a fresh copy</span></p>
<p style="top:402.6pt;left:101.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Not require human intervention to start and run</span></p>
<p style="top:436.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">To drive the adoption of Cloud Native best practices and support and promote the growing </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#0069ff">Cloud </span></b></p>
<p style="top:453.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#0069ff">Native Landscape</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">, the Cloud Native Computing Foundation (CNCF) was created under the </span></p>
<p style="top:470.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">umbrella of the Linux Foundation to foster the growth and development of high-quality projects </span></p>
<p style="top:487.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">like Kubernetes. Examples of other CNCF projects include Prometheus, a monitoring system and </span></p>
<p style="top:504.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">time-series database often rolled out alongside Kubernetes; and FluentD, a data and log collector </span></p>
<p style="top:521.6pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">often used to implement distributed logging in large clusters.</span></p>
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">06</span></p>
<p style="top:584.4pt;left:112.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">In its current charter, the CNCF de&#xfb01;nes three core properties that underpin Cloud </span></p>
<p style="top:603.4pt;left:112.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Native applications: </span></p>
<p style="top:630.4pt;left:132.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Packaging applications into containers: &#x201c;</span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containerizing</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">&#x201d;</span></p>
<p style="top:649.4pt;left:132.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Dynamic scheduling of these containers: &#x201c;</span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">container orchestration</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">&#x201d;</span></p>
<p style="top:668.4pt;left:132.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Software architectures that consist of several smaller loosely-coupled and </span></p>
<p style="top:687.4pt;left:132.8pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">independently deployable services: &#x201c;</span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">microservices</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">&#x201d;</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:85.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Scaling with Kubernetes Case Study: </span></b></p>
<p style="top:111.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">The Snappy Monolith</span></b></p>
<p style="top:153.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">To demonstrate the value of implementing Cloud Native best practices including containerization </span></p>
<p style="top:170.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">along with a microservices architecture, we&#x2019;ll use a running example throughout this paper: a photo </span></p>
<p style="top:187.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">sharing app called Snappy that provides basic photo upload and sharing functionality between </span></p>
<p style="top:204.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">users through a web interface. </span></p>
<p style="top:238.6pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Throughout this paper, we&#x2019;ll modernize Snappy by:</span></p>
<p style="top:272.6pt;left:101.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Decomposing the app&#x2019;s business functions into microservices</span></p>
<p style="top:289.6pt;left:101.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Containerizing the various components into portable and discretely deployable pieces</span></p>
<p style="top:306.6pt;left:101.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Using a DigitalOcean Kubernetes cluster to scale and continuously deploy these </span></p>
<p style="top:323.6pt;left:101.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">stateless microservices</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">07</span></p>
<p style="top:507.8pt;left:96.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LOAD BALANCER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:671.7pt;left:80.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">OBJECT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:682.5pt;left:76.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">STORAGE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:671.7pt;left:149.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">DATABASE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:567.0pt;left:88.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">SNAPPY MONOLITH</span></b></p>
<p style="top:419.7pt;left:113.0pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">INTERNET</span></b></p>
<p style="top:682.8pt;left:460.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">VIRTUAL SERVER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:401.3pt;left:244.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">SNAPPY MONOLITH</span></b></p>
<p style="top:432.7pt;left:311.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">API / WEB UI</span></b></p>
<p style="top:525.4pt;left:293.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">DATABASE ADAPTER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:472.1pt;left:259.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO</span></b></p>
<p style="top:482.9pt;left:259.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MANAGEMENT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:472.1pt;left:356.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">USER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:482.9pt;left:356.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MANAGEMENT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:425.4pt;left:452.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PRESENTATION</span></b></p>
<p style="top:436.2pt;left:452.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LAYER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:471.1pt;left:452.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">BUSINESS</span></b></p>
<p style="top:481.9pt;left:452.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LOGIC</span></b></p>
<p style="top:525.4pt;left:452.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">DB LAYER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:587.9pt;left:261.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">BINS / LIBS / LANGUAGE RUNTIME</span></b></p>
<p style="top:628.4pt;left:261.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">OPERATING SYSTEM</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.0pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">08</span></p>
<p style="top:71.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">With our photo-sharing monolith app Snappy, we observe that at &#xfb01;rst the web UI, photo </span></p>
<p style="top:88.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">management, and user management business functions are combined in a single codebase where </span></p>
<p style="top:105.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">these separate components invoke each other via function calls. This codebase is then built, </span></p>
<p style="top:122.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">tested, and deployed as a single unit, which can be scaled either horizontally or vertically. </span></p>
<p style="top:156.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">As Snappy acquires more users &#x2014; and subsequently scales and iterates on the product &#x2014; the </span></p>
<p style="top:173.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">codebase gradually becomes extremely large and complex. Although code changes and bug &#xfb01;xes </span></p>
<p style="top:190.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">may be minor, the entire monolith app needs to be rebuilt and re-deployed, forcing a slower </span></p>
<p style="top:207.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">iteration cycle. Furthermore, if any individual subcomponent becomes a bottleneck in the </span></p>
<p style="top:224.4pt;left:71.5pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">application, the entire monolith must be scaled as a whole.</span></p>
<p style="top:372.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Microservices</span></b></p>
<p style="top:414.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Microservices is a software architecture style that advocates for many granular services that each </span></p>
<p style="top:431.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">perform a single business function. Each microservice is a self-contained, independently </span></p>
<p style="top:448.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deployable piece of a larger application that interacts with other components, typically via </span></p>
<p style="top:465.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">well-de&#xfb01;ned REST APIs.</span></p>
<p style="top:499.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Microservices evolved as a hybrid of several software development trends and ideas. Some, like </span></p>
<p style="top:516.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Service-Oriented Architectures (SOA), DevOps, and containerization are more recent, while others, </span></p>
<p style="top:533.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">like the Unix philosophy of &#x201c;Do One Thing and Do It Well,&#x201d; evoke principles developed decades </span></p>
<p style="top:550.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">ago. Initially pioneered by large, web-scale internet companies like Google, Amazon, and Netflix, </span></p>
<p style="top:567.1pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">microservices architectures have now become commonplace in applications of all sizes.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:71.3pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Monolithic vs. Microservices Architectures </span></b></p>
<p style="top:97.9pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Large, multi-tier software monoliths must be scaled as a cohesive whole, slowing down </span></p>
<p style="top:114.9pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">development cycles. In contrast, microservices provide several advantages over this </span></p>
<p style="top:131.9pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">inflexible model:</span></p>
<p style="top:165.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">They can be scaled individually and on demand</span></p>
<p style="top:182.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">They can be developed, built, tested and deployed independently</span></p>
<p style="top:199.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Each service team can use its own set of tools and languages to implement features, and </span></p>
<p style="top:216.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">grow at its own rate </span></p>
<p style="top:233.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Any individual microservice can treat others as black boxes, motivating strongly </span></p>
<p style="top:250.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">communicated and well-de&#xfb01;ned contracts between service teams </span></p>
<p style="top:267.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Each microservice can use its own data store which frees teams from a single overarching </span></p>
<p style="top:284.9pt;left:102.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">database schema</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">09</span></p>
<p style="top:461.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Breaking the Monolith: </span></b></p>
<p style="top:487.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Snappy Microservices Architecture</span></b></p>
<p style="top:530.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Looking at Snappy through the lens of a microservices-oriented architecture, we see that </span></p>
<p style="top:547.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">individual business functions such as photo management and user administration have now been </span></p>
<p style="top:564.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">broken out into separate microservices that communicate via REST APIs. Each microservice can </span></p>
<p style="top:581.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">use the data store most appropriate for the type of data it will be handling. For example, the photo </span></p>
<p style="top:598.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">management microservice can use a cloud object store for images along with a traditional </span></p>
<p style="top:615.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">relational database management system (RDBMS) for metadata. The service can then be </span></p>
<p style="top:632.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">developed, tested, deployed, and scaled independently from other services. Allowing for greater </span></p>
<p style="top:649.9pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">development agility, teams leveraging microservices can more ef&#xfb01;ciently use cloud infrastructure.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.5pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">10</span></p>
<p style="top:267.5pt;left:274.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LOAD BALANCER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:179.4pt;left:292.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">INTERNET</span></b></p>
<p style="top:348.3pt;left:259.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI MICROSERVICE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:639.3pt;left:378.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">USER MGMT MICROSERVICE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:416.5pt;left:404.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LOAD BALANCER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:601.6pt;left:427.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">RDBMS</span></b></p>
<p style="top:312.2pt;left:259.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI</span></b></p>
<p style="top:327.3pt;left:258.4pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
<p style="top:312.2pt;left:338.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI</span></b></p>
<p style="top:327.3pt;left:337.3pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
<p style="top:469.7pt;left:393.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">USER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:480.5pt;left:391.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:494.5pt;left:388.7pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
<p style="top:469.7pt;left:471.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">USER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:480.5pt;left:469.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:494.5pt;left:466.9pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
<p style="top:639.3pt;left:113.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO MGMT MICROSERVICE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:604.8pt;left:207.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">RDBMS</span></b></p>
<p style="top:601.6pt;left:128.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">OBJECT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:612.4pt;left:125.0pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">STORAGE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:417.5pt;left:144.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LOAD BALANCER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:469.7pt;left:102.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO</span></b></p>
<p style="top:480.5pt;left:104.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:494.5pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
<p style="top:469.7pt;left:168.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO</span></b></p>
<p style="top:480.5pt;left:170.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:494.5pt;left:167.4pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
<p style="top:469.7pt;left:234.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO</span></b></p>
<p style="top:480.5pt;left:236.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:494.5pt;left:233.6pt;line-height:8.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:8.0pt;color:#0069ff">REST API</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:234.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Containers</span></b></p>
<p style="top:276.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Thus far we&#x2019;ve discussed high-level methodologies and architectures that underpin Cloud Native </span></p>
<p style="top:293.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">applications. We&#x2019;ll now discuss a core technology that allows developers to implement these </span></p>
<p style="top:310.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">broader architectural designs: </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containers.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:342.9pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">What are Containers?</span></b></p>
<p style="top:369.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Containers are a way of packaging </span></p>
<p style="top:386.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">applications with all of their required </span></p>
<p style="top:403.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">dependencies and libraries in a portable and </span></p>
<p style="top:420.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">easily deployable format. Once launched, </span></p>
<p style="top:437.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">these packages provide a consistent and </span></p>
<p style="top:454.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">predictable runtime environment for the </span></p>
<p style="top:471.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containerized application. Taking advantage </span></p>
<p style="top:488.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">of Linux kernel isolation features such as </span></p>
<p style="top:505.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">cgroups</span></tt><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> and </span><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">namespaces</span></tt><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">, container </span></p>
<p style="top:522.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">implementations &#x2014; or runtimes &#x2014; provide a </span></p>
<p style="top:539.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">sandboxed and resource-controlled running </span></p>
<p style="top:556.5pt;left:321.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">environment for applications.</span></p>
<p style="top:588.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Containers vs. Virtual Machines</span></b></p>
<p style="top:615.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Compared to virtual machines, containers are more lightweight and require fewer resources </span></p>
<p style="top:632.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">because they encapsulate fewer layers of the operating system stack. Both provide </span></p>
<p style="top:649.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">resource-limited environments for applications and all their software dependencies to run, but </span></p>
<p style="top:666.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">since containers share the host&#x2019;s OS kernel and do not require separate operating systems, they </span></p>
<p style="top:683.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">boot in a fraction of the time and are much smaller in size.</span></p>
<p style="top:752.1pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">11</span></p>
<p style="top:87.2pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">A microservices architecture lies at the heart of Cloud Native application development as these </span></p>
<p style="top:104.2pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">apps consist of portable, containerized microservices that are scalable and disposable. By </span></p>
<p style="top:121.2pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">breaking up a monolithic application into many &#xfb01;ne-grained, self-contained services &#x2014; each of </span></p>
<p style="top:138.2pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">which can be independently scaled, distributed across regions, and deployed across cloud </span></p>
<p style="top:155.2pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">platforms &#x2014; microservices enable faster development iteration, and increased flexibility in running </span></p>
<p style="top:172.2pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">applications on cloud infrastructure.</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
<p style="top:417.9pt;left:110.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">Bins/Libs</span></b></p>
<p style="top:417.9pt;left:214.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">Bins/Libs</span></b></p>
<p style="top:387.8pt;left:202.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">snappy_web: 1.0</span></b></p>
<p style="top:387.8pt;left:92.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">snappy_photo: 2.4</span></b></p>
<p style="top:463.6pt;left:128.0pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER RUNTIME</span></b></p>
<p style="top:521.0pt;left:136.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">INFRASTRUCTURE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:492.8pt;left:115.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">HOST OPERATING SYSTEM</span></b></p>
<p style="top:345.5pt;left:73.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER INSTANCE</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:752.1pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">12</span></p>
<p style="top:71.4pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Container Runtimes</span></b></p>
<p style="top:99.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Though multiple container runtimes are available, Docker is the most mature, widely supported, </span></p>
<p style="top:117.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and common format, embedded into most container orchestration systems. More recently, the </span></p>
<p style="top:135.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Open Container Initiative (OCI), a Linux Foundation project, has worked to standardize container </span></p>
<p style="top:153.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">formats and runtimes, leading to the development and integration of lightweight and stable </span></p>
<p style="top:171.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">OCI-compliant runtimes such as containerd into orchestration systems. In mid-2018, The </span></p>
<p style="top:189.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes project announced general availability for the more minimal </span><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containerd</span></tt><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> runtime, </span></p>
<p style="top:207.0pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">embedding it into Kubernetes versions 1.10 and above. </span></p>
<p style="top:260.5pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Build and Ship: Dockerizing an Application</span></b></p>
<p style="top:288.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Containerizing an application using Docker &#xfb01;rst involves </span></p>
<p style="top:306.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">writing a container image manifest called a </span><i><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Docker&#xfb01;le</span></i><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">. This &#xfb01;le </span></p>
<p style="top:324.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">describes how to build a container image by de&#xfb01;ning the </span></p>
<p style="top:342.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">starting source image and then outlining the steps required to </span></p>
<p style="top:360.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">install any dependencies (such as the language runtime and </span></p>
<p style="top:378.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">libraries), copy in the application code, and con&#xfb01;gure the </span></p>
<p style="top:396.1pt;left:241.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">environment of the resulting image.</span></p>
<p style="top:432.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Developers or build servers then use the Docker container runtime to build these dependencies, </span></p>
<p style="top:450.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">libraries, and application sources into a binary package called a Docker image. Docker images are </span></p>
<p style="top:468.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">built in ordered layers, are composable, and can be reused as bases for new images. Once built, </span></p>
<p style="top:486.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">these images can be used to start containers on any host with a Docker container runtime. </span></p>
<p style="top:504.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Containers are central to running portable Cloud Native applications because using them naturally </span></p>
<p style="top:522.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">guides development towards the implementation of several core Twelve Factor and Cloud Native </span></p>
<p style="top:540.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">principles. As needed, a given Docker container:</span></p>
<p style="top:576.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Implements some narrow piece of business or support logic</span></p>
<p style="top:594.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Explicitly declares all of its software dependencies in a Docker&#xfb01;le</span></p>
<p style="top:612.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Is extremely portable across cloud providers as long as it has the requisite resources and a </span></p>
<p style="top:630.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Docker runtime</span></p>
<p style="top:648.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Deploys quickly to replace a failed running container of the same type</span></p>
<p style="top:666.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Replicates easily to accommodate the additional load on a heavily requested business </span></p>
<p style="top:684.1pt;left:101.3pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">function by launching additional container instances </span></p>
<p style="top:263.3pt;left:71.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">DOCKERFILE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:293.2pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">FROM</span></b></p>
<p style="top:304.0pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">...</span></b></p>
<p style="top:314.8pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">copy</span></b></p>
<p style="top:325.6pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">run</span></b></p>
<p style="top:336.4pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">expose</span></b></p>
<p style="top:347.2pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">cmd</span></b></p>
<p style="top:358.0pt;left:78.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">...</span></b></p>
<p style="top:293.2pt;left:129.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">node: 10.2.1</span></b></p>
<p style="top:317.3pt;left:129.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">package.json ./</span></b></p>
<p style="top:328.1pt;left:129.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">npm install</span></b></p>
<p style="top:338.9pt;left:129.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">8080</span></b></p>
<p style="top:349.7pt;left:129.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">[&#x201d;npm&#x201d;, &#x201c;start&#x201d;]</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:431.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Building a Snappy Microservice: Web UI </span></b></p>
<p style="top:457.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Container Lifecycle</span></b></p>
<p style="top:500.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">To demonstrate one possible container-based development workflow, we&#x2019;ll zoom in on Snappy&#x2019;s </span></p>
<p style="top:517.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Web UI microservice, an Express and Node.js based web server. </span></p>
<p style="top:603.4pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Develop &amp; Push</span></b></p>
<p style="top:630.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Since this Express app depends on Node.js and its related libraries to run, the </span><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">snappy_web </span></tt></p>
<p style="top:647.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Docker&#xfb01;le &#xfb01;rst sources a Node.js image from a Docker registry like Docker Hub. Further Docker&#xfb01;le </span></p>
<p style="top:664.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">steps include app con&#xfb01;guration, copying in source code &#xfb01;les, and &#xfb01;nally telling Docker which </span></p>
<p style="top:681.0pt;left:72.0pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">command to run when launching the application container.</span></p>
<p style="top:752.1pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">13</span></p>
<p style="top:240.9pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:11.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:11.0pt;color:#10244f">This is where Kubernetes and container orchestration come into play.</span></b></p>
<p style="top:71.4pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Once your team&#x2019;s application has been neatly packaged into a set of microservice containers, each </span></p>
<p style="top:89.4pt;left:72.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">performing some unit of business functionality, you should consider the following questions:</span></p>
<p style="top:125.4pt;left:102.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">How do you then deploy and manage all of these running containers? </span></p>
<p style="top:143.4pt;left:102.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">How do these containers communicate with one another, and what happens if a given </span></p>
<p style="top:161.4pt;left:102.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">container fails and becomes unresponsive? </span></p>
<p style="top:179.4pt;left:102.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">If one of your microservices begins experiencing heavy load, how do you scale the number of </span></p>
<p style="top:197.4pt;left:102.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">running containers in response, assigning them to hosts with resources available? </span></p>
<p style="top:565.2pt;left:79.9pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#0069ff">&lt;/&gt;</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:72.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">A Snappy developer on the web UI team begins work on a small UI bug &#xfb01;x. The developer tests code </span></p>
<p style="top:89.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">changes locally by rebuilding the Express Docker image and running the web server container on </span></p>
<p style="top:106.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">their laptop. The developer, satis&#xfb01;ed with the changes, then pushes the code to a branch in the </span></p>
<p style="top:123.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">team&#x2019;s source code repository.</span></p>
<p style="top:207.3pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Build &amp; Test</span></b></p>
<p style="top:233.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">This push triggers a continuous integration pipeline build. The continuous integration server builds </span></p>
<p style="top:250.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">the Node.js dependencies, libraries, and modi&#xfb01;ed sources into a Docker image. Once built, the </span></p>
<p style="top:267.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">pipeline runs this image as a container and proceeds to execute unit and integration tests.</span></p>
<p style="top:284.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">If all the tests pass, this validated Docker image is then pushed to a container image registry &#x2014; an </span></p>
<p style="top:301.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">abstraction layer typically built on top of object storage &#x2014; for container image tagging, organization, </span></p>
<p style="top:318.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and ef&#xfb01;cient reuse of existing image layers. Private, organization-speci&#xfb01;c container image registries </span></p>
<p style="top:335.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">allow teams to share and publish images to a central, secure location, whereas public registries allow </span></p>
<p style="top:352.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">popular open-source projects like Node.js to make the latest versions of their software available to </span></p>
<p style="top:369.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">developers in prebuilt container image form.</span></p>
<p style="top:453.3pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Deploy &amp; Run</span></b></p>
<p style="top:479.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Now that the Snappy web UI container image containing the bug &#xfb01;x has been approved and pushed </span></p>
<p style="top:496.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">to a registry, a container orchestration system such as Kubernetes can then &#x201c;pull&#x201d; this image and </span></p>
<p style="top:513.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deploy it onto any host with a Docker runtime. This running container is given a narrow view of </span></p>
<p style="top:530.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">available resources speci&#xfb01;ed by the developer, and is run in isolation from other containers. A single </span></p>
<p style="top:547.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">host with a container runtime installed can run several containers simultaneously, depending on </span></p>
<p style="top:564.9pt;left:73.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">available resources.</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
<p style="top:752.1pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">14</span></p>
