<p style="top:290.3pt;left:392.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">snappy_web: 1.0</span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:302.9pt;left:279.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Health Checking and State Management</span></p>
<p style="top:319.9pt;left:279.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Autoscaling</span></p>
<p style="top:336.9pt;left:279.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Rolling Deployments</span></p>
<p style="top:353.9pt;left:279.1pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Declarative Con&#xfb01;guration</span></p>
<p style="top:70.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Clusters</span></b></p>
<p style="top:113.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Adopting a microservices architecture consisting of containerized applications paves the way for </span></p>
<p style="top:130.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">more ef&#xfb01;cient use of infrastructure, close control of application runtime environments, and the </span></p>
<p style="top:147.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">ability to automatically scale. However, one of the major tradeoffs in moving to a </span></p>
<p style="top:164.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">microservices-oriented architecture are the added complexities (e.g. in business logic, </span></p>
<p style="top:181.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">observability, and incident management) in managing a constantly evolving distributed system. </span></p>
<p style="top:198.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Container orchestration systems were designed to reduce some of the operations overhead by </span></p>
<p style="top:215.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">abstracting away the underlying infrastructure and automating the deployment and scaling of </span></p>
<p style="top:232.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containerized applications. Systems such as Kubernetes, Marathon and Apache Mesos, and Swarm </span></p>
<p style="top:249.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">simplify the task of deploying and managing fleets of running containers by implementing some or </span></p>
<p style="top:266.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">all of the following core functionality:</span></p>
<p style="top:302.4pt;left:102.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Container Scheduling</span></p>
<p style="top:320.4pt;left:102.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Load Balancing</span></p>
<p style="top:338.4pt;left:102.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Service Discovery</span></p>
<p style="top:356.4pt;left:102.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Cluster Networking</span></p>
<p style="top:392.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Let&#x2019;s briefly take a look at each of these features:</span></p>
<p style="top:496.8pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Container Scheduling</span></b></p>
<p style="top:523.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">When deploying a container or sets of identical containers, a</span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> scheduler</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> manages allocating the </span></p>
<p style="top:540.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">desired resources (like CPU and memory) and assigns the containers to cluster member nodes </span></p>
<p style="top:557.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">with these resources available. In addition, a scheduler may implement more advanced </span></p>
<p style="top:574.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">functionality like container prioritization, as well as balancing out sets of identical containers across </span></p>
<p style="top:591.4pt;left:72.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">different members and regions for high availability.</span></p>
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">16</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">17</span></p>
<p style="top:119.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Load Balancing</span></b></p>
<p style="top:147.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Once deployed into a cluster, sets of running containers need some load balancing component to </span></p>
<p style="top:164.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">manage the distribution of requests from both internal and external sources. This can be </span></p>
<p style="top:181.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">accomplished using a combination of cloud provider load balancers, as well as load balancers </span></p>
<p style="top:198.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">internal to the container orchestration system.</span></p>
<p style="top:281.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Service Discovery</span></b></p>
<p style="top:308.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Running containers and applications need some way of &#xfb01;nding other apps deployed to the cluster. </span></p>
<p style="top:325.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Service discovery exposes apps to one another and external clients in a clean and organized </span></p>
<p style="top:342.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">fashion using either DNS or some other mechanism, such as local environment variables..</span></p>
<p style="top:425.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Cluster Networking</span></b></p>
<p style="top:452.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Clusters also need to connect running applications and containers to one another across </span></p>
<p style="top:469.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">machines, managing IP addresses and assignment of network addresses to cluster members and </span></p>
<p style="top:486.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containers. Networking implementations vary across container cluster projects; some like Docker </span></p>
<p style="top:503.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Swarm bake a set of networking features directly into the cluster, whereas others like Kubernetes </span></p>
<p style="top:520.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">impose a minimal set of requirements for any networking implementation, allowing administrators </span></p>
<p style="top:537.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">to roll out their own custom overlay network solution.</span></p>
<p style="top:620.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Health Checking and State Management</span></b></p>
<p style="top:648.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">A core feature implemented by Cloud Native applications is health reporting, usually via a REST </span></p>
<p style="top:665.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">endpoint. This allows orchestrators to reliably check the state of running applications and only direct </span></p>
<p style="top:682.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">traf&#xfb01;c towards those that are healthy. Also using this endpoint, orchestrators repeatedly probe </span></p>
<p style="top:699.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">running apps and containers for &#x201c;liveness&#x201d; and self-heal by restarting those that are unresponsive. </span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">18 </span></p>
<p style="top:124.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Autoscaling</span></b></p>
<p style="top:151.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">As load increases on a given application, more containers should be deployed to match this </span></p>
<p style="top:168.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">growth in demand. Container orchestrators handle scaling applications by monitoring standard </span></p>
<p style="top:185.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">metrics such as CPU or memory use, as well as user-de&#xfb01;ned telemetry data. The orchestrator then </span></p>
<p style="top:202.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">increases or decreases the number of running containers accordingly. Some orchestration systems </span></p>
<p style="top:219.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">also provide features for scaling the cluster and adding additional cluster members should the </span></p>
<p style="top:236.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">number of scheduled containers exceed the amount of available resources. These systems can </span></p>
<p style="top:253.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">also monitor utilization of these members and scale the cluster down accordingly, rescheduling </span></p>
<p style="top:270.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">running containers onto other cluster members.</span></p>
<p style="top:338.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> </span></b></p>
<p style="top:353.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Rolling Deployments</span></b></p>
<p style="top:380.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Container orchestration systems also implement functionality to perform zero-downtime deploys. </span></p>
<p style="top:397.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Systems can roll out a newer version of an application container incrementally, deploying a </span></p>
<p style="top:414.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">container at a time, monitoring its health using the probing features described above, and then </span></p>
<p style="top:431.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">killing the old one. They also can perform blue-green deploys, where two versions of the </span></p>
<p style="top:448.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">application run simultaneously and traf&#xfb01;c is cut over to the new version once it has stabilized. This </span></p>
<p style="top:465.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">also allows for quick and painless rollbacks, as well as pausing and resuming deployments as they </span></p>
<p style="top:482.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">are carried out.</span></p>
<p style="top:565.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Declarative Con&#xfb01;guration</span></b></p>
<p style="top:600.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Another core feature of some container orchestration systems is deployment via declarative </span></p>
<p style="top:617.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">con&#xfb01;guration &#xfb01;les. The user &#x201c;declares&#x201d; which desired state they would like for a given application </span></p>
<p style="top:634.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">(for example, four running containers of an NGINX web server), and the system takes care of </span></p>
<p style="top:651.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">achieving that state by launching containers on the appropriate members, or killing running </span></p>
<p style="top:668.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containers. This declarative model enables the review, testing, and version control of deployment </span></p>
<p style="top:685.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and infrastructure changes. In addition, rolling back applications version can be as simple as </span></p>
<p style="top:702.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deploying the previous con&#xfb01;guration &#xfb01;le. In contrast, imperative con&#xfb01;guration requires developers </span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">1 9</span></p>
<p style="top:72.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">to explicitly de&#xfb01;ne and manually execute a series of actions to bring about the desired cluster </span></p>
<p style="top:89.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">state, which can be error-prone, making rollbacks dif&#xfb01;cult.</span></p>
<p style="top:140.9pt;left:70.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Depending on the container orchestration project, some of these features may be implemented </span></p>
<p style="top:157.9pt;left:70.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">with more or less maturity and granularity. Whether it&#x2019;s Apache&#x2019;s Mesos and Marathon, Docker&#x2019;s </span></p>
<p style="top:174.9pt;left:70.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Swarm, or Kubernetes, a container orchestration system greatly facilitates running scalable and </span></p>
<p style="top:191.9pt;left:70.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">resilient microservices on cloud platforms by abstracting away the underlying infrastructure and </span></p>
<p style="top:208.9pt;left:70.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">reducing operational complexity.</span></p>
<p style="top:242.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Rolling out cluster software to manage your applications often comes with the cost of </span></p>
<p style="top:259.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">provisioning, con&#xfb01;guring, and maintaining the cluster. Managed container services like </span></p>
<p style="top:276.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">DigitalOcean Kubernetes can minimize this cost by operating the cluster Control Plane and </span></p>
<p style="top:293.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">simplifying common cluster administration tasks like scaling machines and performing </span></p>
<p style="top:310.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">cluster-wide upgrades.</span></p>
<p style="top:344.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">As open-source container clusters and their managed equivalents have evolved and gradually </span></p>
<p style="top:361.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">taken on large-scale production workloads, Kubernetes and its expanding ecosystem of Cloud </span></p>
<p style="top:378.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Native projects have become the platform of choice for managing and scheduling containers. By </span></p>
<p style="top:395.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">implementing all of the features described above, Kubernetes empowers developers to scale </span></p>
<p style="top:412.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">alongside their success, and managed Kubernetes offerings provide them with even greater </span></p>
<p style="top:429.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">flexibility while minimizing DevOps administration time and software operations costs.</span></p>
<p style="top:506.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes</span></b></p>
<p style="top:548.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">The Kubernetes container orchestration system was born and initially designed at Google by </span></p>
<p style="top:565.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">several engineers who architected and developed Google&#x2019;s internal cluster manager Borg. These </span></p>
<p style="top:582.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">engineers sought to build and open-source a container management system that integrated many </span></p>
<p style="top:599.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">of the lessons learned from developing this internal container platform. Since its July 2015 v1.0 </span></p>
<p style="top:616.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">release, Kubernetes has rapidly matured and been rolled out in large production deployments by </span></p>
<p style="top:633.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">organizations such as Bloomberg, Uber, eBay, and also here at DigitalOcean. In March 2018, </span></p>
<p style="top:650.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes became the &#xfb01;rst project to graduate from the Cloud Native Computing Foundation, </span></p>
<p style="top:667.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">indicating that it has become mature and stable enough to handle large-scale production </span></p>
<p style="top:684.9pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deployments and has achieved a high level of code quality and security.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">20</span></p>
<p style="top:71.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Beyond implementing all of the container cluster features listed above (and many more), </span></p>
<p style="top:88.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes bene&#xfb01;ts from a thriving open-source community, which actively develops new features </span></p>
<p style="top:105.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and provides constant feedback and bug reporting across a variety of deployments and use cases. </span></p>
<p style="top:122.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">In addition to Kubernetes features, this growing developer community continuously builds tools </span></p>
<p style="top:139.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">that simplify the process of setting up, con&#xfb01;guring, and managing Kubernetes clusters.</span></p>
<p style="top:173.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Before discussing DigitalOcean Kubernetes and how it enables developers to rapidly deploy their </span></p>
<p style="top:190.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">containerized Cloud Native applications into a managed cluster, we&#x2019;ll &#xfb01;rst dive into the design and </span></p>
<p style="top:207.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">architecture of the Kubernetes system and discuss some of the core features that simplify </span></p>
<p style="top:224.5pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deploying and scaling applications.</span></p>
<p style="top:298.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Kubernetes Design Overview</span></b></p>
<p style="top:340.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Kubernetes is a container cluster, a dynamic system that manages the deployment, management, </span></p>
<p style="top:357.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">and interconnection of containers on a fleet of worker servers. These worker servers where </span></p>
<p style="top:374.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">containers run are called </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Nodes</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> and the servers that oversee and manage these running containers </span></p>
<p style="top:391.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">are called the Kubernetes </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Control Plane</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">.</span></p>
<p style="top:440.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Containers and Pods</span></b></p>
<p style="top:467.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">It&#x2019;s important to note here that the smallest deployable unit in a Kubernetes cluster is not a </span></p>
<p style="top:484.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">container but a </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Pod.</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> A Pod typically consists of an application container (like a Dockerized </span></p>
<p style="top:501.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Express/Node.js web app), or an app container and any &#x201c;sidecar&#x201d; containers that perform some </span></p>
<p style="top:518.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">helper function like monitoring or logging. Containers in a Pod share storage resources, a network </span></p>
<p style="top:535.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">namespace, and port space. A Pod can be thought of as a group of containers that work together </span></p>
<p style="top:552.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">to perform a given function. They allow developers to ensure that these sets of containers are </span></p>
<p style="top:569.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">always scheduled onto Nodes together.</span></p>
<p style="top:618.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Scaling, Updating and Rolling Back: Kubernetes Deployments</span></b></p>
<p style="top:645.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Pods are typically rolled out using </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Deployments,</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> which are objects de&#xfb01;ned by YAML &#xfb01;les that </span></p>
<p style="top:662.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">declare a particular desired state. For example, an application state could be running three replicas </span></p>
<p style="top:679.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">of the Express/Node.js web app container and exposing Pod port </span><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">8080</span></tt><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">. Once created, a </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">controller </span></b></p>
<p style="top:696.0pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">on the Control Plane gradually brings the actual state of the cluster to match the desired state </span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:791.9pt">
<p style="top:72.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">declared in the Deployment by scheduling containers onto Nodes as required. Using Deploy-</span></p>
<p style="top:89.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">ments, a service owner can easily scale a set of Pod replicas horizontally or perform a zero-down-</span></p>
<p style="top:106.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">time rolling update to a new container image version by simply editing a YAML &#xfb01;le and performing </span></p>
<p style="top:123.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">an API call (e.g. by using the command line client </span><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">kubectl</span></tt><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">). Deployments can quickly be rolled </span></p>
<p style="top:140.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">back, paused, and resumed.</span></p>
<p style="top:189.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Exposing your Application: Kubernetes Services</span></b></p>
<p style="top:216.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Once deployed, a</span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> Service</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> can be created to allow groups of similar deployed Pods to receive </span></p>
<p style="top:233.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">traf&#xfb01;c (Services can also be created simultaneously with Deployments). Services are used to grant </span></p>
<p style="top:250.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">a set of Pod replicas a static IP and con&#xfb01;gure load balancing between them using either cloud </span></p>
<p style="top:267.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">provider load balancers or user-speci&#xfb01;ed custom load balancers. Services also allow users to </span></p>
<p style="top:284.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">leverage cloud provider &#xfb01;rewalls to lock down external access.</span></p>
<p style="top:333.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Pod Management: Kubernetes Node Agents</span></b></p>
<p style="top:360.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">To start and manage Pods and their containers on worker machines, Nodes run an agent process </span></p>
<p style="top:377.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">called </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">kubelet</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> which communicates with a </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">kube-apiserver</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> on the Control Plane. Using a </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">contain-</span></b></p>
<p style="top:394.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">er runtime</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> like Docker, also running on Nodes, these scheduled containers are &#xfb01;rst pulled as </span></p>
<p style="top:411.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">images from either a private or public image registry, and then created and launched. Nodes also </span></p>
<p style="top:428.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">run a kube-proxy, which manages network rules on the host.</span></p>
<p style="top:477.8pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#2d5fea">Control and Schedule: Kubernetes Control Plane</span></b></p>
<p style="top:504.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">The Kubernetes Control Plane oversees the Nodes and manages their scheduling and maintains </span></p>
<p style="top:521.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">their workloads. It consists of the </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">kube-apiserver</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> front-end, backed by the key-value store </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">etcd</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> to </span></p>
<p style="top:538.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">store all the cluster data. Finally, a </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">kube-scheduler</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea"> schedules Pods to Nodes, and a set of </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">control-</span></b></p>
<p style="top:555.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">lers </span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">continuously observe the state of the cluster and drive its actual state towards the </span></p>
<p style="top:572.4pt;left:71.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#2d5fea">desired state.</span></p>
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">21</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">22</span></p>
<p style="top:180.8pt;left:362.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTROLLER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:252.0pt;left:367.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">API SERVER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:320.6pt;left:367.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">SCHEDULER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:276.3pt;left:507.0pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">ETCD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:133.4pt;left:303.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">KUBERNETES CONTROL PLANE</span></b></p>
<p style="top:201.1pt;left:71.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">DEVOPS</span></b></p>
<p style="top:623.8pt;left:91.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE 1</span></b></p>
<p style="top:623.8pt;left:139.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE 2</span></b></p>
<p style="top:623.8pt;left:190.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE 3</span></b></p>
<p style="top:623.8pt;left:240.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE ...</span></b></p>
<p style="top:623.8pt;left:331.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE N</span></b></p>
<p style="top:178.3pt;left:141.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CLI (KUBECTL)</span></b></p>
<p style="top:247.7pt;left:141.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI </span></b></p>
<p style="top:258.5pt;left:141.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">(DASHBOARD)</span></b></p>
<p style="top:404.6pt;left:77.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">cADVISOR</span></b></p>
<p style="top:404.6pt;left:145.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">KUBE-PROXY</span></b></p>
<p style="top:404.6pt;left:228.0pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">KUBELET</span></b></p>
<p style="top:404.6pt;left:338.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">cADVISOR</span></b></p>
<p style="top:404.6pt;left:406.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">KUBE-PROXY</span></b></p>
<p style="top:404.6pt;left:489.0pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">KUBELET</span></b></p>
<p style="top:443.4pt;left:81.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:467.2pt;left:81.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:514.8pt;left:69.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD 1 </span></b></p>
<p style="top:492.3pt;left:171.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:514.8pt;left:158.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD 2 </span></b></p>
<p style="top:443.4pt;left:209.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:490.4pt;left:209.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:467.2pt;left:200.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD 3 </span></b></p>
<p style="top:514.8pt;left:200.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD 4 </span></b></p>
<p style="top:539.2pt;left:81.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER RUNTIME</span></b></p>
<p style="top:539.2pt;left:342.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER RUNTIME</span></b></p>
<p style="top:136.7pt;left:146.0pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#0069ff">&gt;_</span></b></p>
<p style="top:443.2pt;left:340.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:467.0pt;left:340.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:514.6pt;left:329.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD </span></b></p>
<p style="top:443.2pt;left:426.4pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CONTAINER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:467.0pt;left:416.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.2pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">23</span></p>
<p style="top:71.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">This brief high-level architectural overview demonstrates that Kubernetes provides advanced and </span></p>
<p style="top:88.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">extensible functionality for deploying and running containerized applications on cloud </span></p>
<p style="top:105.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">infrastructure. However, provisioning, con&#xfb01;guring, and managing a Kubernetes cluster, and </span></p>
<p style="top:122.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">integrating existing CI/CD pipelines and automation servers often requires non-trivial lead and </span></p>
<p style="top:139.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">maintenance time for operators and DevOps engineers. Managed Kubernetes solutions like </span></p>
<p style="top:156.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">DigitalOcean Kubernetes allow development teams to quickly provision a fully featured </span></p>
<p style="top:173.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes cluster on which they can launch their containerized workloads. This means that </span></p>
<p style="top:190.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">software teams can spend more time building applications and less time managing integration, </span></p>
<p style="top:207.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deployment, and the infrastructure that apps run on.</span></p>
<p style="top:267.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">DigitalOcean Kubernetes</span></b></p>
<p style="top:309.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><i><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#64686c">Features described in this section will be ready for use when DigitalOcean Kubernetes </span></i></p>
<p style="top:326.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><i><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#64686c">is generally available.</span></i></p>
<p style="top:360.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">DigitalOcean Kubernetes provides a simple and cost-effective solution for developers seeking to </span></p>
<p style="top:377.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">deploy and run their containerized applications on a Kubernetes cluster. With DigitalOcean, </span></p>
<p style="top:394.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">developers can quickly launch their containerized workloads into a managed, self-healing </span></p>
<p style="top:411.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes environment without having to provision, install, and manage a cluster from scratch.</span></p>
<p style="top:445.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Rolling your own production-ready Kubernetes cluster often involves several time-consuming and </span></p>
<p style="top:462.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">costly steps: provisioning the underlying compute, storage, and networking infrastructure for the </span></p>
<p style="top:479.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Control Plane and Nodes; bootstrapping and con&#xfb01;guring Kubernetes components like the etcd </span></p>
<p style="top:496.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">cluster and Pod networking; and thoroughly testing the cluster for resiliency towards infrastructure </span></p>
<p style="top:513.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">failures. Once set up, Kubernetes clusters need to be managed and monitored by DevOps teams, </span></p>
<p style="top:530.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">while routine maintenance tasks like upgrading the cluster or the underlying infrastructure requires </span></p>
<p style="top:547.0pt;left:71.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">manual intervention by engineers.</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">24</span></p>
<p style="top:86.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Completing the Shift to Cloud Native: </span></b></p>
<p style="top:112.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:20.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:20.0pt;color:#10244f">Snappy on DigitalOcean Kubernetes</span></b></p>
<p style="top:155.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">The Snappy team has evaluated DigitalOcean Kubernetes and decided they would like to roll out </span></p>
<p style="top:172.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">their microservices-based photo sharing application onto the platform. Running on Kubernetes, </span></p>
<p style="top:189.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Snappy consists of the following three Pods (it&#x2019;s helpful to think of each as a microservice):</span></p>
<p style="top:223.9pt;left:100.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Web UI</span></p>
<p style="top:240.9pt;left:100.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Photo Management</span></p>
<p style="top:257.9pt;left:100.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">User Management</span></p>
<p style="top:291.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Once the cluster has been provisioned with the desired number of Nodes, Snappy&#x2019;s developers </span></p>
<p style="top:308.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">create Kubernetes Services and Deployments for each microservice component, referencing </span></p>
<p style="top:325.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Docker images from their private registry. Using Kubernetes Secrets, they can store database </span></p>
<p style="top:342.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">credentials and other sensitive information that they would like Pods to have access to in their </span></p>
<p style="top:359.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">environment. </span></p>
<p style="top:393.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Subsequently, they could then use kubectl or their preferred Kubernetes management tool to </span></p>
<p style="top:410.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">launch the Services into their cluster. Once launched, DigitalOcean Kubernetes will automatically </span></p>
<p style="top:427.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">provision and con&#xfb01;gure remaining cloud infrastructure such as Block Storage, Load Balancers and </span></p>
<p style="top:444.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Firewalls, as declared by the developer.</span></p>
<p style="top:478.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Service owners can then independently scale their services by &#xfb01;rst increasing the number of replica </span></p>
<p style="top:495.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Pods in the Deployment con&#xfb01;guration &#xfb01;le, and then launching the deployment using the </span></p>
<p style="top:512.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes API. This same flow can be automated and integrated with a CI/CD pipeline to </span></p>
<p style="top:529.9pt;left:70.7pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">continuously roll out new versions of the application.</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:612.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">25</span></p>
<p style="top:257.8pt;left:262.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">LOAD BALANCER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:187.8pt;left:439.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">KUBERNETES</span></b></p>
<p style="top:198.6pt;left:449.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">CLUSTER</span></b></p>
<p style="top:140.7pt;left:279.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">INTERNET</span></b></p>
<p style="top:318.0pt;left:129.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:351.1pt;left:129.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">USER MGMT POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:384.1pt;left:129.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO MGMT POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:413.5pt;left:114.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE 2</span></b></p>
<p style="top:433.7pt;left:302.8pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:467.8pt;left:282.3pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE 3</span></b></p>
<p style="top:319.2pt;left:356.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">WEB UI </span></b></p>
<p style="top:330.0pt;left:356.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:366.6pt;left:330.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">NODE 3</span></b></p>
<p style="top:319.2pt;left:415.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO MGMT </span></b></p>
<p style="top:330.0pt;left:415.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">POD</span></b></p>
<p style="top:580.1pt;left:264.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">SPACES</span></b></p>
<p style="top:590.9pt;left:236.5pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">(OBJECT STORAGE)</span></b></p>
<p style="top:580.1pt;left:364.6pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">PHOTO MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:590.9pt;left:379.1pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">RDBMS </span></b></p>
<p style="top:580.1pt;left:138.9pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">USER MGMT</span></b></p>
<p style="top:590.9pt;left:149.2pt;line-height:9.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:ProximaNova,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">RDBMS </span></b></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:613.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:70.0pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Simple, Flexible Scaling</span></b></p>
<p style="top:96.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Development teams using DigitalOcean Kubernetes can quickly create managed clusters for </span></p>
<p style="top:113.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">workloads of all sizes &#x2014; from a single Node, single Pod web server to a massive set of Nodes with </span></p>
<p style="top:130.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">continuously churning compute-intensive processing pods. Regardless of the size or number of </span></p>
<p style="top:147.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">running applications, cluster creation and operation remains simple via a streamlined web </span></p>
<p style="top:164.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">interface and REST API, allowing developers to quickly launch and scale a managed Kubernetes </span></p>
<p style="top:181.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">cluster. Users can de&#xfb01;ne </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">custom con&#xfb01;gurations</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> of standard and compute-optimized Droplets to </span></p>
<p style="top:198.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">handle variable workloads, optimizing price-to-performance and maximizing the use of </span></p>
<p style="top:215.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">underlying resources.</span></p>
<p style="top:265.0pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Minimizing Day 2 Cost: Managed Operations and Maintenance</span></b></p>
<p style="top:291.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Automated cluster upgrades</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> and </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Control Plane backup and recovery</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> further reduce operations </span></p>
<p style="top:308.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and day-to-day management overhead. Teams can quickly integrate the latest security and </span></p>
<p style="top:325.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">performance improvements from the Kubernetes community while keeping their clusters available </span></p>
<p style="top:342.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">to run workloads and remaining resilient to failure. DigitalOcean Kubernetes clusters </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">self-heal </span></b></p>
<p style="top:359.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">automatically</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> &#x2014; Control Plane and Node health are continuously monitored, and recovery and Pod </span></p>
<p style="top:376.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">rescheduling occurs in the background, preventing unnecessary and disruptive off-hours alerts.</span></p>
<p style="top:426.0pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Kubernetes in the DigitalOcean Cloud</span></b></p>
<p style="top:452.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">DigitalOcean Kubernetes </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">integrates seamlessly with other DigitalOcean infrastructure products</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">, </span></p>
<p style="top:469.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">bringing in all the cloud primitives needed to handle scaling and securing your team&#x2019;s applications. </span></p>
<p style="top:486.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">When creating a Service to expose your app, DigitalOcean Kubernetes can </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">automatically </span></b></p>
<p style="top:503.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">provision a Load Balancer</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> and route traf&#xfb01;c to the appropriate Pods. Additionally, you&#x2019;ll be able to </span></p>
<p style="top:520.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">set up a DigitalOcean Firewall</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> to lock down and restrict web traf&#xfb01;c to your running applications. </span></p>
<p style="top:537.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Finally, DigitalOcean </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Block Storage Volumes</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> can be used as </span><tt><span style="font-family:AndaleMono,monospace;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">PersistentVolumes</span></tt><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> to provide </span></p>
<p style="top:554.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">non-ephemeral and highly available shared storage between containers.</span></p>
<p style="top:604.0pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Harness the Kubernetes Ecosystem</span></b></p>
<p style="top:630.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">By fully exposing the Kubernetes Control Plane API, developers have </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">complete control</span></b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f"> over </span></p>
<p style="top:647.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">workload deployment, scaling, and monitoring. Container images can be pulled directly from </span></p>
<p style="top:664.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">public and private registries like Docker Hub and Quay.io, granting teams complete flexibility in </span></p>
<p style="top:681.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">designing and implementing continuous integration and deployment pipelines. With this exposed </span></p>
<p style="top:698.6pt;left:74.2pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">API, developers can also bene&#xfb01;t from the rich ecosystem of third-party Kubernetes tools, as well as </span></p>
<p style="top:753.3pt;left:576.7pt;line-height:9.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:9.0pt;color:#10244f">26</span></p>
<p style="top:754.6pt;left:291.1pt;line-height:7.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:7.0pt;color:#10244f">RUNNING CLOUD NATIVE APPLICATIONS ON DIGITALOCEAN KUBERNETES</span></p>
</div>
<div id="page0" style="width:613.0pt;height:792.0pt">
<p style="top:70.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">build their own implementation-speci&#xfb01;c tooling should no existing solution meet their needs. In </span></p>
<p style="top:87.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">addition, operations teams can quickly leverage the Kubernetes Dashboard UI as well as </span></p>
<p style="top:104.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Prometheus &#x2014; built-in to DigitalOcean Kubernetes &#x2014; for out-of-the-box cluster monitoring </span></p>
<p style="top:122.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">and troubleshooting.</span></p>
<p style="top:173.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">Simple, Transparent Pricing</span></b></p>
<p style="top:200.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">Using DigitalOcean Kubernetes, software teams can maximize their cloud resource utilization and </span></p>
<p style="top:217.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">accurately forecast spend with transparent, predictable pricing. Paying only for running Nodes, </span></p>
<p style="top:234.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">teams have their bandwidth pooled at the account level, making DigitalOcean Kubernetes a market </span></p>
<p style="top:251.0pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:10.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:10.0pt;color:#10244f">leading price-to-performance container platform.</span></p>
<p style="top:353.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">DigitalOcean Kubernetes supports development teams in quickly reaping the </span></p>
<p style="top:372.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">bene&#xfb01;ts provided by Cloud Native computing patterns. Helping teams as they </span></p>
<p style="top:391.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">build containerized, microservices-oriented applications that are designed to run </span></p>
<p style="top:410.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">on the cloud, DigitalOcean Kubernetes reduces time to market and facilitates the </span></p>
<p style="top:429.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">scaling of products and iteration of features. This streamlined, fully-managed, </span></p>
<p style="top:448.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">CNCF-conformant platform runs all kinds of production container workloads. Your </span></p>
<p style="top:467.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">team will experience increased development velocity while fully leveraging the </span></p>
<p style="top:486.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">flexibility offered by cloud infrastructure. DigitalOcean Kubernetes provides you </span></p>
<p style="top:505.4pt;left:74.4pt;line-height:12.0pt"><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#10244f">with </span><b><span style="font-family:Sailec,serif;font-size:12.0pt;color:#0069ff">simplicity as you scale.</span></b></p>
